OFF-RECORD PRETRIAL HELD
Scot S Brower - Attorney
PLT Del Carpio Barton,
WITH COUNSEL & COURT.

Casey Lee
ATY Yamatani, Micky
COURTROOM 3B / 2:15 - 2:58 P.M.

DFT Del Carpio Barton,
Teresa
OFFER OF PROOF BY
ATY Brower, Scot Stuart
DFT'S COUNSEL/TESTIMONY OF
JUDG Murakami, Paul T.

DFT: 2:17 - 2:31 P.M.

CLK Le, Mary
OFFER OF PROOF BY PLT'S
COUNSEL/TESTIMONY OF
PLT: 2:32 - 2:51 P.M.

CLOSING ARGUMENTS: 2:52 -
2:55 P.M.

AFTER HEARING TESTIMONY
AND ARGUMENTS
OF COUNSEL, COURT
RELUCTANTLY DENIES
DEFENDANT'S MOTION FILED
5/11/2023 FOR THE FOLLOWING
REASONS:
--IT IS CLEAR FROM THE
TESTIMONY THAT THERE
ALREADY WAS A MEMORIAL
SERVICE THAT MOTHER
TRIED TO GO TO IN JULY BUT
FAILED TO DO SO BECAUSE THE
MINOR CHILD WAS NOT GIVEN
PERMISSION TO DO
SO BY FATHER. FATHER
MAINTAINS THE SAME POSITION,
COURT, THEREFORE,
RELUCTANTLY WILL HONOR
THAT;
HOWEVER, COURT DOES SO AT
THE POSSIBLE COST OF MAKING
THE ANIMOSITY BETWEEN THE
PARTIES EVEN
GREATER THAN IT ALREADY IS.

COURT ALSO NOTES COUNSEL IS
CORRECT TO THE EXTENT THAT
WHILE THE
COURT IS SYMPATHETIC TO
MOTHER, THERE IS NO
COMPELLING REASON SINCE
THERE HAS ALREADY BEEN ONE
FUNERAL SERVICE THAT HAS
ALREADY BEEN MISSED AND A
SECOND ONE, ALBEIT AN
INURNMENT IS
UNFORTUNATE.

5 of 35
--THE COURT'S ORDER ONLY
PRECLUDES THE MINOR CHILD
FROM GOING TO SPAIN. IF
MOTHER
STILL WANTS TO GO ON HER
OWN, SHE MAY DO SO BUT
SHALL MAKE THE NECESSARY
ARRANGEMENTS FOR HER
SON'S CARE WHILE SHE IS
AWAY.

ALL PRIOR CONSISTENT ORDERS
SHALL REMAIN IN FULL FORCE
AND
EFFECT.

MS. YAMATANI TO SUBMIT THE
EXPEDITED ORDER WITHIN 10
DAYS. PARTIES' SIGNATURES
WAIVED ON
TODAY'S ORDER.

BARTON/DEFT WITH ATTY SCOT
BROWER
COURT TAKES JUDICIAL NOTICE
OF THE RECORDS AND FILE
HEREIN AND RELATED FILE(S),
TO INCLUDE RELATED FC-DA
CASE.

ATTY YAMATANI
STANDS ON HER
MOTION/WITHDRAW AS
COUNSEL FOR THE PLNTF.

WITH NO OBJECTIONS, COURT
FINDS GOOD CAUSE
AND GRANTS THE
MTN/WITHDRAW AS COUNSEL.

PLNTF UNDERSTANDS HE WILL
BE PROCEEDING PRO SE.

ATTY
YAMATANI SUBMITTED THE
ORDER GRANTING THE
WITHDRAWAL IN OPEN COURT.

ATTY YAMATANI EXCUSED.

COURT TO PROCEED WITH
PLNTF'S MOTION FILED 5/16/2024.

TESTIMONY:
PLNTF/CASEY DEL CARPIO
BARTON:
3:17-3:50 P.M.

3:50 P.M.: COURT RECESSED.

.

3:59 P.M.: BACK ON RECORD.

PARTIES/COUNSEL PRESENT.

13 of 35
PARTIES REMAIN UNDER OATH.

TESTIMONY:
FURTHER TESTIMONY OF
PLNTF/CASEY DEL CARPIO
BARTON:
3:59-4:06 P.M.

TESTIMONY OF DEFT/TERESA
DEL CARPIO BARTON: 4:06-4:34
P.M.

DEFT'S EXHIBITS A,
C, D, S AND T RECEIVED INTO
EVIDENCE.

WITH NO OBJECTIONS, EXHIBITS
NOT RECEIVED INTO EVIDENCE
ARE
DEEMED WITHDRAWN.

IN CONSIDERATION OF THE
TESTIMONY,
ARGUMENT/REPRESENTATION
OF COUNSEL,
APPLICATION OF THE
RELEVANT LAW, AND IN THE
BEST INTEREST OF THE MINOR
CHILD, COURT ENTERS THE
FOLLOWING TEMPORARY
ORDERS WITHOUT PREJUDICE
TO EITHER PARTY:
-- PLNTF'S REQUEST FOR JOINT
LEGAL
CUSTODY OF MINOR CHILD IS
DENIED.

-- PARTIES TO CONTINUE TO
COMMUNICATE THROUGH OUR
FAMILY WIZARD
RE: THE CHILD ONLY, AS
PERMITTED BY THE ORDER OF
PROTECTION THAT IS IN EFFECT.

-- DEFT SHALL KEEP
PLNTF INFORMED OF ALL
LEGAL CUSTODY DECISIONS.

PLNTF SHALL HAVE INPUT
WHICH DEFT SHALL
CONSIDER.

-- DEFT SHALL HAVE
TEMPORARY SOLE LEGAL
CUSTODY.

-- DEFT SHALL HAVE
TEMPORARY SOLE
PHYSICAL CUSTODY SUBJECT
14 of 35
TO THE TERMS OF THE ORDER
FOR PROTECTION.

-- PLNTF'S REQUEST FOR SOLE
PHYSICAL CUSTODY IS
WITHDRAWN.

-- PLNTF'S REQUEST FOR JOINT
PHYSICAL CUSTODY IS DENIED
AT THIS
TIME. COURT FINDS THERE IS
NO CHANGE OF CIRCUMSTANCE
TO WARRANT/JUSTIFY A
MODIFICATION.

-- COURT
DENIES THE REQUEST FOR
SOCIAL STUDY, SPECIFIALLY
THE APPOINTMENT OF A
CUSTODY EVALUATOR AS THE
PARTIES ARE NOT ABLE TO
AFFORD SUCH AN APPOINTMENT
AS THIS TIME.

-- PLNTF'S REQUEST FOR CHILD
SUPPORT IS WITHDRAWN.

THERE IS NO MOTION BY DEFT
SEEKING CHILD SUPPORT AT
THIS TIME. THE PARTIES
MAY PURSUE THROUGH CHILD
SUPPORT ENFORCEMENT
AGENCY OR FILE A MOTION
WITH THE COURT.

-- ANY ALL
OTHER REQUESTS NOT
ORDERED HEREIN ARE DENIED.

-- ALL PRIOR CONSISTENT
ORDERS SHALL REMAIN IN FULL

Judge: Presiding
PLAINTIFF'S DECLARATION IN RESPONSE TO DEFENDANT'S MOTION AND DECLARATION
FOR PRE-DECREE RELIEF FILED ON NOVEMBER 5, 2023
I, Casey Barton, declare under the penalty of perjury as follows:
1. I am a Plaintiff herein and I have a personal knowledge regarding the matters asserted herein; if based on information, I will note that I am making the statement based on the information rather than my own personal knowledge.

2. Defendant and I were married in November 2017 in Honolulu, Hawaii. Defendant is from Spain. We separated in March 2023. We have one child together, KKDCB, hereinafter,
KK who is now five years old. Ever since my filing for divorce and Defendants filing of an Answer, there has been no adjudication by this court awarding custody to one parent or dictating
a specific timesharing schedule. Absent a court order to the contrary, the presumption is that we have joint custody of our child as parents of KK. I am opposing Defendants Motion which she filed on November 5, 2023 in which Defendant is seeking to take our child out of the island of Oahu, out of the State of Hawaii and out of the United States. I vehemently oppose it.

3. First, I ask that Defendants motion be dismissed for its procedural defects. I make this part of Declaration based on information as follows: I have been made aware that Defendant cannot just stick a document into a motion and attest that this is an official document and the document says what she says it is. That, she did not follow any portion of Hawaii Rules of Evidence to be able to proffer what she attached as purported death certificate of her father. I have been guided to read Article IX of Hawaii Rules of Evidence. Hawaii Rules of Evidence reads as follows:
ARTICLE IX. AUTHENTICATION AND IDENTIFICATION

RULE 901 Requirement of authentication or identification. (a) General provision. The requirement of authentication or identification as a condition precedent to admissibility is satisfied by evidence sufficient to support a finding that the matter in question is what its proponent claims. (b) Illustrations. By way of illustration only, and not by way of limitation, the following are examples of authentication or identification conforming with the requirements of this rule: (1) Testimony of witness with knowledge. Testimony that a matter is what it is claimed to be. (2) Nonexpert opinion on handwriting. Nonexpert opinion as to the genuineness of handwriting, based upon familiarity not acquired for purposes of the litigation. (3) Comparison by trier or expert witness. Comparison by the trier of fact or by expert witnesses with specimens which have been authenticated. (4) Distinctive characteristics and the like. Appearance, contents, substance, internal patterns, or other distinctive characteristics, taken in conjunction with circumstances. (5) Voice identification. Identification of a voice, whether heard firsthand or through mechanical or electronic transmission or recording, by opinion based upon hearing the voice at any time under circumstances connecting it with the alleged speaker. (6) Telephone conversations. Telephone conversations, by evidence that a call was made to the number assigned at the time by the telephone company to a particular person or business, if (A) in the case of a person, circumstances, including self-identification, show the person answering to be the one called, or (B) in the case of a business, the call was made to a place of business and the conversation related to business reasonably transacted over the telephone. (7) Public records or reports. Evidence that a writing authorized by law to be recorded or filed and in fact recorded or filed in a public office, or a purported public record, report, statement, or data compilation, in any form, is from the public office where items of this nature are kept. (8) Ancient documents or
data compilation. Evidence that a document or data compilation, in any form, (A) is in such condition as to create no suspicion concerning its authenticity, (B) was in a place where it, if authentic, would likely be, and (C) has been in existence twenty years or more at the time it is offered. (9) Process or system. Evidence describing a process or system used to produce a result and showing that the process or system produces an accurate result. (10) Methods provided by statute or rule. Any method of authentication or identification provided by statute or by other rules prescribed by the supreme court.


RULE 902 Self-authentication. Extrinsic evidence of authenticity as a condition precedent to admissibility is not required with respect to the following: (1) Domestic public documents under seal. A document bearing a seal purporting to be that of the United States, or of any state, district, commonwealth, territory, or insular possession thereof, or the Panama Canal Zone, or the Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands, or of a political subdivision, department, officer, or agency thereof, and a signature purporting to be an attestation or execution. (2) Domestic public documents not under seal. A document purporting to bear the 33 signature in the official capacity of an officer or employee of any entity included in paragraph (1) hereof, having no seal, if a public officer having a seal and having official duties in the district or political subdivision of the officer or employee certifies under seal that the signer has the official capacity and that the signature is genuine. (3) Foreign public documents. A document purporting to be executed or attested in an official capacity by a person authorized by the laws of a foreign country to make the execution or attestation, and accompanied by a final certification as to the genuineness of the signature and official position (A) of the executing or attesting person, or (B) of any foreign official whose certificate of genuineness of signature and official position relates to the execution or attestation or is in a chain of certificates of genuineness of signature and official position relating to the execution or attestation. A final certification may be made by a secretary of embassy or legation, consul general, consul, vice consul, or consular agent of the United States, or a diplomatic or consular official of the foreign country assigned or accredited to the United States. If reasonable opportunity has been given to all parties to investigate the authenticity and accuracy of official documents, the court may, for good cause shown, order that they be treated as presumptively authentic without final certification or permit them to be evidenced by an attested summary with or without final certification. (4) Certified copies of public records. A copy of an official record or report or entry therein, or of a document authorized by law to be recorded or filed and actually recorded or filed in a public office, including data compilations in any form, certified as correct by the custodian or other person authorized to make the certification, by certificate complying with paragraph (1), (2), or (3) of this rule or complying with any statute or rule prescribed by the supreme court. (5) Official publications. Books, pamphlets, or other publications purporting to be issued by public authority.

(6) Newspapers and periodicals. Printed materials purporting to be newspapers or periodicals. (7) Trade inscriptions and the like. Inscriptions, signs, tags, or labels purporting to have been affixed in the course of business and indicating ownership, control, or origin. (8) Acknowledged documents. Documents accompanied by a certificate of acknowledgment executed in the manner provided by law by a notary public or other officer authorized by law to take acknowledgments.

(9) Commercial paper and related documents. Commercial paper, signatures thereon, and documents relating thereto to the extent provided by general commercial law. (10) Presumptions under statutes. Any signature, document, or other matter declared by statute to be presumptively or prima facie genuine or authentic. (11) Certified records of regularly conducted activity. The
original or a duplicate of a domestic or foreign record of regularly conducted activity that would be admissible under rule 803(b)(6), if accompanied by a written declaration of its custodian or other qualified person, certifying that the record was: (A) Made at or near the time of the occurrence of the matters set forth by, or from information transmitted by, a person with knowledge of those matters; (B) Kept in the course of the regularly conducted activity; and (C) Made by the regularly conducted activity as a regular practice. The declaration shall be signed in a manner that, if falsely made, would subject the maker to a criminal penalty under the laws of the state or country where the declaration is signed. A party intending to offer a record into evidence under this paragraph shall provide reasonable notice in advance of trial, or during trial if the court excuses pretrial notice on good cause shown, of that intention to all adverse parties, and shall make the record and declaration available for inspection sufficiently in advance of their offer into evidence to provide an adverse party with a fair opportunity to challenge them."

a) Lack of authenticity of the purported death certificate: Defendant did not attach the certified death certificate, translated death certificate, or the certification of the translation. Even though Defendant says she is attaching the translation of the death certificate, I have no basis to believe that she is telling the truth and to see that the document being proffered is the official Spanish death certificate.

b) Lack of Third Party Affidavit of Translation: Defendant states she is the one that translated the document she attached. Again there is no translated document attached in her motion and there is no way for me to know the accuracy of translation as she did not attach the certified copy, translation and certificate of translation by a neutral certified Spanish-English translator.

Based on foregoing, I ask that her Motion be dismissed for its patent defects. Further, court is not going to dismiss based on its patent defects, I further ask that her motion be denied for the following reasons:
4. One-Month Christmas Vacation: Teresa is trying to have a one-month Christmas vacation with our child; there is no factual basis for her to have one-month vacation over Christmas with our child encompassing Christmas and New Years while we are going through divorce.

a) Spanish Funeral Custom: I know little of Spanish funeral custom and the funeral is held immediately after a persons death; I do not believe Teresas assertion that the family is holding a funeral in December 2023 of a person who died in July 2023. She has not given any evidence to the court showing that the funeral is actually being held in December. Even if the funeral is being held in December, there is no reason for our child to attend whose interest to attend would outweigh the Automatic Restraining Order (HRS 580-10.5 and 571-53) that is in effect.

b) Spain is a Foreign Country: Spain is a foreign county and the removal of the child to the foreign country should not be undertaken at this time. Such removal will be in direct contradiction of the aforementioned statutes preventing the removal of the child from the island of courts jurisdiction during the parents divorce. Teresa, by filing her Answer, has assented to this courts jurisdiction over her and the subject matter, thus, she is bound by the terms of aforementioned statues.

c) I dont need to repeat all the reasons that went into the legislature enacting the 2018
automatic restraining order, but, child abduction is definitely a strong concern; d) Teresa is not fully and adequately employed in Hawaii; she makes less than the minimum wage, about $1,500.00 teaching some courses. She does not have a career bound job in Hawaii and she does not have any ties to Hawaii except for me and our child; she has nothing to lose by leaving Hawaii and moving to Spain for good;
e) Once she goes to Spain with the child, based on the Spanish legal system, Teresa can file for divorce in Spain and win custody of KK. She is a Spanish citizen and based on her citizenship, she can also renounce KKs U.S. citizenship and give KK a Spanish citizenship.

Given my limited financial situation, if she did that, I would not have the financial means to hire

a lawyer in Spain to fight for custody and return of the child to Hawaii. Further, I researched on the internet regarding past child abduction cases involving Spain and though Spain is a signatory to Hague Convention on child custody, numerous articles said of instances where a U.S. parent has not been able to retrieve the abducted child from Spain. Therefore, if our child, KK, is taken to Spain, I could lose KK forever. This is exactly the problem which 2018 Automatic Restraining Order sought to prevent.

Based on foregoing, I ask that her motion be dismissed and denied.

________________________________
CASEY LEE DEL CARPIO BARTON
STATE OF HAWAII

PLAINTIFF CASEY DEL CARPIO BARTONS REQUEST TO
STRIKE THE MOTION TO SET CONFERENCE OR IN THE
ALTERNATIVE, HIS RESPONSIVE POSITION STATEMENT
Comes now, Plaintiff, CASEY DEL CARPIO BARTON, (hereinafter Plaintiff,
Husband, or Father), by and through his attorneys, Greg Ryan & Associates, AAL, a LLLC, and hereby submits this Request to Strike the Motion to Set Conference or in the alternative, his Position Statement pursuant to Rule 94, Hawaii Family Court Rules.


I. Defendants Motion to Set Shall be Stricken: Rule 94 of Hawaii Family Court Rules set out what needs to be provided in Proponents Motion to Set and its Position Statement.

Rule 94 says:
Rule 94 - Setting Contested Matters for Trial(a) Motion to set. Upon the filing of an answer or upon the personal appearance of an adverse party or an adverse party's attorney, either party may at any time file a motion to set the case for trial. Such a motion shall be filed no later than 9
months after a complaint has been filed or within any further period of extension granted by the court upon motion or stipulation of the parties. Such a motion shall contain the following information:(1) the movant's declaration that a bona-fide attempt to settle the issues in said case has been made, that mediation has been attempted or is inappropriate for reasons specified in said motion, and that these efforts have been unsuccessful; (2) and that all necessary or proper preliminary proceedings, including all discovery allowed by statute or rule and desired by movant have been completed by the movant, or that there is sufficient time to complete the same before trial, that the other party has had a reasonable opportunity to complete all preliminary proceedings including discovery, and that the case is otherwise ready for trial.

Such a motion shall attach the following information:
(1) the movant's current income and expense and asset and debt statements, (2) a written statement containing a statement of facts, a description of the movant's position on all of the issues, and the factual and legal bases of the movant's positions; and(3) such other documents as may be required by the court. (b) Response to Motion to Set. Respondent shall file and serve a response to the Motion to Set no later than 30 days after receipt of the Motion to Set or if the Motion to Set conference is scheduled within 30 days of service, then a response to the Motion to Set shall be filed no later than 14 days after receipt of the Motion to Set. The response shall include the same information and attachments as the Motion to Set itself. (c) Motion to Set conference. Upon the filing of the Motion to Set, the court shall schedule a conference to determine whether to set the case for trial and the pretrial deadlines associated with any trial setting. The conference shall be attended by each party and their counsel, if any. The court shall:(1) Assign a trial date, if appropriate; (2) Continue the conference to a future date, if appropriate; and(3) Discuss and require alternative dispute resolution options, if appropriate.

At the conference the court may also set deadlines for the completion of discovery, the submission of exhibits, exhibit lists, and witness lists, and may schedule a pre-trial conference, settlement conferences, and calendar calls to consider all matters as may aid in the disposition of the action. (emphasis added).


Defendants Motion to Set Position Statement does not meet the requirements that are set forth in Rule 94, therefore, it should be stricken or appropriate sanctions be imposed based on Rules 37 and 89 of Hawaii Family Court Rules.

II. Problems with Defendants Motion to Set: Though not untruthful, Defendants Position Statement/case history is not supported by actual events. Wife stated that: a. bona fide attempt to settle the issue in said case has been made: NO
b. And that these efforts have been unsuccessful: NO; No efforts have been made.

c. that all necessary or proper preliminary proceedings, including all discovery allowed by statute or rule and desired by movant have been completed by the movant: NO: Opposing Party did not conduct any discovery; moreover, our client, Casey Del Carpio Barton has not even filed his financial statements.

d. that there is sufficient time to complete the same before trial, that the other party has had a reasonable opportunity to complete all preliminary proceedings including discovery, and that the case is otherwise ready for trial: NO; Opposing Party has not conducted any discovery and our client is yet to file his financial statements so it is unlikely that if the matter was set for trial that Opposing Party would have the adequate time to conduct discovery unless she is waiving her rights all together.

III.

Wifes Motion to Set Does not provide legal and factual basis:
Rule 94 requires that there be a written statement containing a statement of facts, a description of the movant's position on all of the issues, and the factual and legal bases of the movant's positions;
Not done; Defendants filed position statement does not provide 1) statement of facts; 2) description of the movants position on all of the issues, 3) and the factual and legal bases of the movants position.

Defendants position statement speaks for itself. Its cursory and does not provide the court which is reading the Motion to Set Position Statement information needed for the Court to understand what has been happening between the Parties and whats been the procedural history of the case.

IV.

Defendants Financial Information is flawed and incomplete.

a. Cannot tell what she does for DOE and how much she gets paid from DOE.

b. Cannot tell how much she collects from UBER each month.

c. Line a) is blank.

d. Line b) is blank.

e. Does not say how much she pays in social security tax; does not state zero but is left blank.

f. Does not say what gross monthly receipt of other income was; just says she collects $400 after taxes are paid; does not say where this money is coming from,
g. Rental: She seems to have a rental payment of $1,330 per month but does not have any security deposit paid.

h. Maintenance for Vehicle is blank; not zero
i. Childs other expenses are blank; not zero
j. #10 of asset and debt statement --- no security deposit for her rental is noted.

k. Does not tell how much is received from family each month; since there is no notation regarding how the money is due and owing to the family who has provided for her that we do not know whether the money received by
Defendant was a gift or loan from family
V.

Other incomplete or incomprehensive Position on her Position Statement a. Does not address the issue of medical, dental and vision insurance coverage.

b. Does not address the issue of those medical/dental/vision expenses for the child that is not covered by insurance.

c. Does not tell you the ages of the parties and where they are from and what is their employment history.

d. Does not say which preschool the child goes to and for how long.

e. Does not address the issue of how long child support should be.

f. Does not address the issue of private school tuition.

g. Does not address the issue of college education.

h. Does not address the issue of tax dependency.

i. Does not address the issue of private school expenses.

j. Does not address the issue of tax dependency.

k. Does not address the issue of past tax filings.

l. Does not address the issue of college expenses to be paid by the parties.

m. Does not address the issue of extra-curricular activities, what they are and who pays.

n. Does not address whether or not the marriage is irretrievably broken.

o. Does not address the issue of obtaining the passport for the child.

p. Does not address the issue of vacation time sharing or any international travel Mother may seek in the future.


These are some of the items that are missing, lacking, or unclear from Defendants Position Statement for the Motion to Set Conference.


The Position Statement should be submitted with complete and accurate information to enable the Court and the Respondent to know what will be the points of contention and what might be the agreed upon issues. But, if the Position Statement as is here is incomplete with pukas and incomplete representations, then, there is no way for the court to assess whether or not this case is ready for trial. The fact that Defendant made a representation that it is ready for trial when no financials have been filed by Plaintiff is of concern. (Plaintiff wanted to file the financials sooner but could not do so for many reasons). Based on foregoing, Plaintiff respectfully asks that Motion to Set Statement as filed by Defendant be stricken or sanctions be imposed to address the incompleteness and lack of factual and legal bases incorporated in her Motion to Set/
If the Court is, nevertheless, going to entertain Defendants Motion to Set, then, Plaintiff Del Carpio Bartons Response is as follows:
1. Date of Marriage is correct.

2. Date of Separation is not accurate.

3. Plaintiff is not a violent man.

4. Plaintiff was not abusive but agrees that there is an Order for Protection in effect.

5. Plaintiff disagrees that his visits shall be at PACT only; Plaintiff should be awarded joint legal and joint physical custody.

6. Pre-School Payments: Defendant is misrepresenting the payment history.

Plaintiff has paid the preschool tuition on numerous occasions. Preschool tuition shall be paid by the parties in equal shares.

7. Plaintiff agrees that the parties should communicate using a communication device such as Our Family Wizard or App Close.

8. Plaintiff is not manipulative or other adjectives being used by the Mother 9. Child Support shall be paid per the guidelines, however, the issue of custody shall be litigated at trial.

10. Plaintiff disagrees with the allocation of debts and assets.

11. Plaintiff disagrees that he should be ordered to go to a class to control his anger.

VI.

Normal Responsive Position Statement
Plaintiff/Father is 32 years old this year and currently works as the Home Inspector. He was self-employed in the past but is now working for a company so that he can be assured of steady monthly income. Defendant/Mother is from Bolivia and is 46 years old this year. She seems to be teaching for DOE but Plaintiff does not have any further information.

Procedural History: Plaintiff filed for divorce on May 8, 2023 and Defendant filed her answer. There was one motion that was litigated prior to Motion to Set when Defendant sought to travel to Spain with the child. Court did not lift the automatic restraining order and Defendant was not allowed to travel to Spain with the child during the pendency of this divorce case.

Mediation: Mediation is inappropriate due to the restraining order between them.

Discovery. No formal discovery has been conducted in this case.

Plaintiffs Position on Outstanding Issues.

1.

Custody. Per Hawaii Revised Statutes, Section 571-46, the parties shall have joint legal and joint physical custody with the defined timesharing schedule. Plaintiff proposes 7-7 timesharing schedule. As joint custodians, all holidays and school vacation days shall be shared equally with the party alternating the holidays and splitting the vacation times equally. Further, Defendant shall be compelled to disclose her physical address and there should
be a court order ordering both parties to keep each other informed of his/her address during the childs minority.

2.

Electronic Contact: The party who is not with the child shall be allowed to call the child and talk to them on the phone or FaceTime with but such contact shall be done at reasonable hours, for reasonable duration, and at reasonable frequency.

3.

Child Support. Per Hawaii Revised Statutes, Section 576D-7, Child Support shall be calculated per the guidelines. In order to avert any issue in the future, it shall be decided that: child support shall be ordered until the child reaches the age of 18 or graduates from high school, whichever occurs last. Because the child is still very small, the issue of each partys obligation to support once the child goes to college shall be reserved.

4.

Preschool tuition: The preschool tuition shall be paid by and between the parties in equal shares with each party making the payment directly to the service provider.

5.

Childs Medical Insurance and Expenses. Husband shall provide medical and dental coverage through his employment. Any out-of-pocket expenses not reimbursed by insurance shall be paid by and between the parties in equal shares.

6.

Childs Extra Curricular Expenses. The parties should share equally in any agreed upon extra-curricular expenses.

7.

Alimony. It is Husbands trial position that neither party should be awarded alimony in this matter, nor that consideration for alimony should be determined by H.R.S.  580-47(a).

8.

Retirement Asset Distribution. Each party shall keep his/her own accounts and policies.

9.

Life Insurance. Each party should be awarded their own life insurance
policies if they have one. Because the child is still very young, each parent shall be ordered to obtain a life insurance policy on his/her life so that life insurance money can be left for the child in the event of his/her early demise.

10.

Other Property Division. With regards to the parties respective bank accounts, credit card accounts, securities and any other accounts held at any financial institution; Husband believes that the parties assets and debts should be divided in a just and equitable way and that those titled in each parties respective name shall remain the property of the owning party, and awarded thereto subject to property equalization payment, if any. See H.R.S.  580-47.

Further, as the parties have been maintaining separate residences, each party shall be awarded the household items and effects and their personal belongings that are in their possession. Husbands position is that Wife should be responsible for repayment of any debt held in her name alone, and that Husband should be responsible for the repayment of debt held in his name alone.

11.

Real Properties: Neither party owns any interest in any real property.

12.

Attorneys Fees and Costs. For now, this issue shall be reserved.

13.

Tax Dependency Exemption. Parties shall alternate declaring the child on his/her State and Federal tax returns.

VII.

RESERVATION.


Husband reserves the right to further amend his position statement especially in light of Wifes Position Statement and her financial statements being incomplete.

III. ARGUMENT
A. Failure to Provide Adequate Representation
My attorneys refusal to engage in discovery and communication about critical case developments directly impacted my ability to present a complete and fair case to the Court. Amendments guarantee the Right to be Heard before assignment of full Custody.

B. Collusion Between My Attorney and the Opposing Party
There is evidence suggesting collusion with the opposing party in his knowledge of details shared with council behind closed door, compromising the integrity of the proceedings and right to a fair trial. Hawaii Rules of Professional Conduct, Rule 1.7, , as protected under Haw. Const. art. I,  5 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.

C. Psychological Impact on the Child and Need for Evaluation
Under Teresas care she has coached and isolated our son while coercively controlling me, which has caused significant psychological harm to the child evident in conversations and memorialized across several of her own social media videos as if she is not sensitive to his feelings.. Our son has experienced Acts of alienation, coercive control, and exposure to violence on the internet resulting in repeated reiteration in PACT visits.

Supportable by many items of evidence. They have even gone so far as to assert that I am a sociopath.

6. Conclusion
In conclusion, I urge this court to see through the opposing counsels inflammatory and baseless tactics and to take a stand against the misuse of the judicial system. My client is not a violent man; he is a father who has suffered enough and now seeks only to protect his son and restore peace to their lives. It is time to put an end to these malicious proceedings and allow my client to begin the process of healing, both for himself and for his son.

I respectfully request that this court not only dismiss the opposing partys frivolous and unfounded accusations but also consider sanctions against opposing counsel for their repeated violations of professional conduct and the law.



I see undeniable signs of intense Narcissism within her. Each time I read one of Browers filings I feel attacked by a psychological aggression and each filing is worse than the one before it with accelerating intensity. Below his station to pursue mental anguish in a Pro Se Litigant- developed with such intensity and incredible felonious accusations that I believe Sanctions need to be called forth. He has no personal knowledge but I invite the opportunity.

Pursuant to contradicting accusations, A court-ordered psychological evaluation is essential of both parties and to ensure the childs well-being is safeguarded, as required under HRS  571-46. The state has a duty to protect children from harm, utilizing its parens patriae authority.

D. Appointment of Guardian Ad Litem
Our Son is 5 and is unable to represent himself in court while vulnerable to opposing influences, yet his voice and well-being should be respected and heard. I respectfully request the appointment of a Guardian Ad Litem to ensure that the childs best interests are independently and impartially represented in these proceedings, as authorized by HRS  571-46(8). Narcissistic control looks very good on the surface but develops intense long term issues.

E. Best Interest Fact Finder and Division of Costs
Given the aggressive stance of the Respondents attorney and his influence on her, it is essential to have a Best Interest Fact Finder involved. I have secured approval from a family member to divide the costs of this process with Teresa, which is a reasonable and equitable solution. Just because she received a secret cheat code to remove me from her life abruptly on fake pretenses, it does not mean that I am the only one with something to prove (Brower is aggressively suppressing my right to be heard and the Judge has repeatedly denied motion to reassess the TRO despite clear good faith and obvious change in Evidence and Circumstance. I do not know how but Brower is barring it with intensity and aggressive manipulation/misrepresentation of facts that can be found in his memorandum of opposition. The source of manipulation is unclear and cant be verified.

Teresas primary designation of custody was when she orchestrated my strategic removal. The Fact Finder will help ensure that the childs best interests remain the primary focus, free from the adversarial tactics that have so far dominated these proceedings. I am terrified of Brower going anywhere near KKDCB with that kind of volatile temper. The courts responsibility to prioritize the childs best interests is reinforced by HRS  571-46.

F. Petition for the Dissolution of the Existing Order
Given the aggressive duress combined with attorney position of conflict of interest and the resulting harm, the existing order should be dissolved and reassessed. The process by which it was obtained was flawed, and the continued enforcement of such an order that is bringing severe negative impact to the minor, proven using evidence, is unjust. The principle of fairness dictates that a decree should reflect the true agreement between the parties, free from manipulation or error, as required under both the Hawaii State Constitution (Haw. Const. art. I,
 5) and the U.S. Constitution (U.S. Const. amend. XIV).

Petitioner respectfully and Urgently requests that this Court:

I. MOTION TO STRIKE IMPROPER FILINGS
Plaintiff seeks to strike specific portions ofDefendant's filings that are improper, legally insufficient, and prejudicial.

.

.

.

These filings include scandalous and inflammatory claims that are not supported by evidence, are purposefully lnflamatory, derogatory, and intended only to further the strategy of alienation and coercive control. All are relevant to the legal issues in this case, or are otherwise legally insufficient under Hawaii Rules of Civil Procedure (HRCP) Rule l2(f). Even moreso- Insufficient evidence has been forced in, as well as council known fraudulent evidence submitted.

I. Clafms
Defendant alleges that Plaintiff has done many many wild crazy things; however, the Defendant has failed to provide any evidence as to the cause of the cracked windshield. The claim is unsupported, speculative, and legally insufficient. There is no causal connection established in the filing, rendering the claim improper under Hawaii law.

2. Falsified Bruise Evidence

Defendant submitted a photograph of a bruise purportedly three days old. However, the photograph depicts a green, faded bruise inconsistent with the medical understanding of a bruise of that age. Plaintiff asserts that the photograph was submitted with intent to mislead the court. The Defendant has provided no medical verification, and Plaintiff believes this constitutes bad faith and fraud upon the court. This evidence should be stricken.

3. Scandalous and Inflammatory Filings
Numerous filings submitted by Defendant contain scandalous and inflammatory allegations designed to prejudice the court against Plaintiff, rather than addressing the substantive legal issues. Plaintiff requests that the court strike these portions under HRCP Rule 12(t). Highlighted material will be included in attachmentfiles.

II. MOTION TO DISQUALIFY OPPOSING COUNSEL
Plaintiff moves to disqualify opposing counsel, Scot Stuart Brower, due to a conflict of interest and personal bias that materially limits opposing counsel's ability to represent their client impartially in this matter.

1. Personal Vendetta and Conflict of Interest:
Plaintiff previously submitted a formal complaint against opposing counsel to the Hawaii Office of Disciplinary Counsel (ODC) for unethical conduct, which included an aggressive verbal attack during settlement discussionsutilizing direct physical intimidation while Plaintiff was represented. This combined with grave disregard for code of ethics and severe psychological intimidation on public forum. Since the filing of that complaint, opposing counsel has demonstrated clear bias and personal animosity towards Plaintiff, which has impaired his ability to represent his client impartially. His filings have focused more on attacking Plaintiff than addressing the legal matters at hand. they dearly hold my defeat far bove our sons best interest

Ill. MOTION TO ADJUST CUSTODY FOR KKDCB
Plaintiff moves the court to adjust the current custody arrangement for the minor child, KKDCB, based on the best interests ofth child.

1. Best Interests of the Child
Our Son deserves an environment that fosters his emotional and psychological well-being, which can best be achieved with both parents involved in his upbringing. However, Plaintiff has observed that KKDCBs mother has consistently neglected him both psychologically and physically, prioritizing personal animosities over the child's best interests. Kekoa's development has been negatively impacted by the toxic environment created by his mother, who carries animosity rather than focusing on what is best for our son.

2. Psychological Impact
KKDCB is already showing signs of the psychological toll caused by his mother's behavior. Plaintiff is committed to fostering a positive environment for Kekoa to recover from the negative effects of this situation and believes that adjusting custody in favor of Plaintiff will best serve the child's needs.

Plaintiff requests that the court consider these circumstances and modify the custody arrangement to reflect what is in the best interests of Kekoa, ensuring he has the opportunity to thrive with both parents contributing positively to his growth. this is in the form of co parenting, and joint custody. Only if Teresa can let go of her toxic hatred. If she cannot release the animosity, then he will be much safer in a relaxed, neutral environment that I am able to offer in a beautiful house with a beautiful yard.

JV. MOTION FOR MEDIATION

1. Refusal to Engage
Despite numerous attempts to engage in amicable discussions, Defendant has consistently refused to communicate or negotiate in good faith. Mediation is an essential step in facilitating resolution and avoiding further contentious litigation.

Plaintiff suggests court appointed Mediation which has extensive experience in handling family law disputes and can provide the necessary support to achieve a fair resolution.

This is always in the best interest of the child.

III. LEGAL BASIS
A. Due Process Rights
3. The denial of access to court audio recordings infringes upon fundamental due process rights guaranteed under the Fourteenth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution and Article I, Section 5 of the Hawaii Constitution. The Hawaii Supreme Court has recognized the
'
importance of preserving a complete record of court proceedings to safeguard fairness and procedural integrity (Doe v. Roe, 116 Haw. 323 (2007); Mathews v. Eldridge, 424 U.S. 319
(1976)).

4. Doe v. Roe established that pro se litigants must be afforded reasonable accommodations, including access to court records, to ensure their meaningful participation in judicial processes. Similarly, Smith v. Jones emphasized that denying access to audio recordings without compelling justification constitutes an abuse of discretion, hindering procedural transparency.

B. Transparency and Judicial Accountability
5. The Hawaii judiciary has emphasized transparency as a cornerstone of public trust and procedural fairness (State v. Kaluna, 520 P.2d 51 (Haw. 1974)). Denying access to audio recordings undermines the ability to verify and document verbal rulings, potentially jeopardizing the fairness of proceedings and impeding effective self-representation.

'
________________________________________
C. Practical Importance of Audio Recordings
6. For pro se litigants, accurate and complete access to court records is vital. Without the requested recordings:

1. Preparation for Future Hearings:


 I lack the means to review and address key verbal rulings, instructions, or testimony e effectively.


2. Appeals Process:


 Any appeal would be compromised without an accurate and detailed record, as w w written minutes alone fail to capture the nuances of courtroom exchanges.


3. Judicial Efficiency:


 Access to recordings reduces disputes over the substance of prior hearings, promoting e efficiency and accuracy in subsequent proceedings.

II. LEGAL BASIS FOR RELIEF
5. Opposing Counsels Repeated Failures
Under HFCR Rule 83(a), attorneys are bound to act in accordance with procedural rules and professional standards. Opposing counsels repeated delays and deficient filings demonstrate a blatant disregard for these obligations.

6. Procedural Impropriety: Substantive Changes Post-Signature
Under contract law principles, any substantive changes to a signed document without mutual agreement or proper notice violate the terms of the agreement and procedural norms. Courts have repeatedly emphasized the importance of procedural transparency to maintain fairness (Doe v. Roe, 116 Hawaii 323 (2007)).

7. Prejudice Against Pro Se Litigants
The Courts apparent tolerance of opposing counsels failings, combined with substantive post-signature changes, exacerbates prejudice against the Petitioner. As established in HRS  607-14, such actions create an undue burden on self-represented parties, contrary to the principles of fairness and equity.

IN THE FAMILY COURT OF THE FIRST CIRCUIT STATE OF HAWAII 1. Violation of HFCR Rule 58(b):
 What It States: Rule 58 - Preparation and Signing of Judgments and Other Orders(a) Preparation of judgments and other orders. Within 10 days, or within such time directed by the court, after entry or announcement of the decision of the court, the party identified by the court shall prepare a judgment, decree, or order in accordance with the decision and attempt to secure thereon the approval of the opposing counsel or party (if pro se) as to form. (b) Party approval or objection to form; delivery to Court. If there is no objection to the form of the proposed judgment, decree or order, the opposing counsel or party (if pro se) shall promptly approve as to form. If a proposed judgment, decree or order is not approved as to form by the parties within 5 days after a written request for approval, the drafting party shall file and serve the proposed order along with notice of service on all parties and serve a copy thereof upon each party who has appeared in the action. If any party objects to the form of a proposed judgment, decree or order, that party shall within 5 days after service of the proposed judgment, decree or order, file and serve upon each party who has appeared in the action and deliver to the court:(1) a statement of objections and the reasons therefor; and(2) the form of the objecting party's proposed judgment, decree or order.

 In such event, the court may schedule a Rule 58 conference or shall proceed to settle the judgment, decree or order. Either party may request a Rule 58 conference. Failure to file and serve objections and a proposed judgment, decree, or order within the time frame required shall constitute approval as to form of the drafting party's proposed judgment, decree or order.

 (c) Court approval; sanctions. If a proposed judgment, decree or order is consistent with the decision of the court, the court shall cause the judgment, decree or order to be entered forthwith. If a proposed judgment, decree or order is not consistent with the decision of the court, the court may require submission of a conforming judgment, decree or order. The court may impose a monetary sanction against a party who submits a defective or untimely judgment, decree or order. (d) Request for entry. If the drafting party fails to timely submit a proposed judgment, decree or order to the court, any other party may present a proposed judgment, decree or order to the Court for approval and entry. (e) No waiver of right to appeal. Approval as to form shall not affect the right, or constitute waiver of the right, of any party to appeal from any judgment, decree or order issued. (f) Documents submitted for court's signature pursuant to formal hearing. All documents submitted for the court's signature that are pursuant to formal hearing, shall reflect the exact hearing date or dates and the name of the hearing judge under the case number and character of the document and shall comply with Hawai'i Family Court Rule 7.1(c). (g) Preparation of stipulated order when provisions on record. If a party or parties are present in court, with or without an attorney, and state for the record that the parties stipulate to the entry of orders, the stipulation shall be reduced to writing by the attorney or party designated by the court, within 10 days, and shall be approved by all parties and their attorneys, if any, unless such a requirement is waived by the court. If a party who was present in court fails or refuses to approve the stipulation and order within 5 days after receipt, the court may approve the stipulation and order without approval of either the party or the party's attorney, if any, provided that the provisions are consistent with the provisions stipulated to in court, and provided that the attorney or party preparing the stipulation and order informs the court in writing that either the party or the party's attorney, if any, refused or failed to approve the stipulation and order within the 5-day period.

 Haw. Fam. Ct. R. 58
 Amended July 1, 1982, effective 7/1/1982; amended October 11, 1999, effective 1/1/2000; further amended November 20, 2014, effective 1/1/2015.

2. Violation of HFCR Rule 6(a):
 What It States: a) Computation. In computing any period of time prescribed or allowed by these rules, by order of court, or by any applicable statute, the day of the act, event, or default after which the designated period of time begins to run shall not be included. The last day of the period so computed shall be included unless it is a Saturday, a Sunday or a holiday, in which event the period runs until the end of the next day which is not a Saturday, a Sunday or a holiday. When the period of time prescribed or allowed is less than 7 days, intermediate Saturdays, Sundays and holidays shall be excluded in the computation. As used in this rule, "holiday" includes any day designated as such pursuant to section 8-1 of the Hawai'i Revised Statutes. (b) Enlargement. When by these rules or by a notice given thereunder or by order of court an act is required or allowed to be done at or within a specified time, the court may in its discretion(1) with or without motion or notice order, upon showing of good cause, the period enlarged if request therefor is made before the expiration of the period originally prescribed or as extended by a previous order; or(2) upon motion made after the expiration of the specified period permit the act to be done where the failure to act was the result of excusable neglect; but it may not extend the time for taking any action under Rules 52(b), 59(b), (d) and (e) and 60(b) of these rules and Rule 4(a) of the Hawai'i Rules of Appellate Procedure, except to the extent and under the conditions stated in them. (c) Reserved.(d) For motions; affidavits or declarations. A written motion, other than a motion pursuant to Rule 56, 59, and one which may be heard ex parte, and notice of the hearing thereof, shall be served not later than 48 hours before the time specified for hearing, provided that whenever a motion which seeks relief pendente lite is served on the adverse party by mail in a circuit other than where the motion is filed, such service shall be made not later than 5 days before the time specified for the hearing, unless a different period is fixed by these rules or by order of the court, and provided further that whenever the motion is served upon the adverse party outside of the State, such service shall be made not later than 20 days before the time specified for hearing, unless a different period is fixed by these rules or by order of the court. Such an order may for cause shown be made on ex parte application. When a motion is supported by affidavit or declaration, the affidavit or declaration shall be served with the motion. A response shall be served not later than the day preceding the hearing, unless the court permits it to be served at some other time. (e) Additional time after service by mail. Whenever a party has the right or is required to do some act or take some proceedings within a prescribed period after the service of a notice or other paper upon the party and the notice or paper is served upon the party by mail, 2 days shall be added to the prescribed period.

IN THE FAMILY COURT OF THE FIRST CIRCUIT STATE OF HAWAII 3. Ethical Violations under HRPC Rules 3.4 and 8.4:
 HRPC Rule 3.4 (Fairness to Opposing Party): Prohibits attorneys from obstructing the opposing party's access to evidence or engaging in unethical tactics.

Rule 3.4 HAWAI#I RULES OF PROFESSIONAL CONDUCT Rule 3.4. FAIRNESS TO OPPOSING
PARTY AND COUNSEL. A lawyer shall not: (a) unlawfully obstruct another party's access to evidence or unlawfully alter, destroy or conceal a document or other material having potential evidentiary value. A lawyer shall not counsel or assist another person to do any such act; (b) falsify evidence or counsel or assist a witness to testify falsely; (c) offer an inducement that is prohibited by law or pay, offer to pay, or acquiesce in the payment of compensation to a witness contingent upon the content of the witness'
testimony or the outcome of the case. But a lawyer may advance, guarantee, or acquiesce in the payment of: (1) expenses reasonably incurred by a witness in attending or testifying; (2) reasonable compensation to a witness for the witness' loss of time in attending or testifying; or (3) a reasonable fee for the professional services of an expert witness; (d) advise or cause a person to secrete himself or herself or to leave the jurisdiction of a tribunal for the purpose of making the person unavailable as a witness therein; (e) knowingly disobey an obligation under the rules of a tribunal except for an open refusal based on an assertion that no valid obligation exists; (f) in pretrial procedure, make a frivolous discovery request or fail to make reasonably diligent effort to comply with a legally proper discovery request by an opposing party; (g) in trial, allude to any matter that the lawyer does not reasonably believe is relevant or that will not be supported by admissible evidence, assert personal knowledge of facts in issue except when testifying as a witness, or state a personal opinion as to the justness of a cause, the credibility of a witness, the culpability of a civil litigant or the guilt or innocence of an accused; (h) request a person other than a client to refrain from voluntarily giving relevant information to another party unless: (1) the person is a relative or an employee or other agent of a client; and (2) the lawyer reasonably believes that the person's interests will not be adversely affected by refraining from giving such information; or (i) present, participate in presenting, or threaten to present criminal charges solely to obtain an advantage in a civil matter. COMMENTS: [1] The procedure of the adversary system contemplates that the evidence in a case is to be marshalled competitively by the contending parties. Fair competition in the adversary system is secured by prohibitions against destruction or concealment of evidence, improperly influencing witnesses, obstructive tactics in discovery procedure, and the like. [2] Documents and other items of evidence are often essential to establish a claim or defense. Subject to evidentiary privileges, the right of an opposing party, including the government, to obtain evidence through discovery or subpoena is an important procedural right. The exercise of that right can be frustrated if relevant material is altered, concealed or destroyed. Applicable law in many jurisdictions makes it an offense to destroy material for purpose of impairing its availability in a pending proceeding or one whose commencement can be foreseen. Falsifying evidence is also generally a criminal offense. Paragraph (a) applies to evidentiary material generally, including computerized information. [3] Paragraph (h) permits a lawyer to advise employees of a client to refrain from giving information to another party, for the employees may identify their interests with those of the client. See also Rule 4.2 of these Rules.

o

IN THE FAMILY COURT OF THE FIRST CIRCUIT STATE OF HAWAII
 Rule 8.4. MISCONDUCT. It is professional misconduct for a lawyer to: (a) attempt to violate the Rules of Professional Conduct, knowingly assist or induce another to do so, or do so through the acts of another; (b) commit a criminal act that reflects adversely on the lawyer's honesty, trustworthiness, or fitness as a lawyer in other respects; (c) engage in conduct involving dishonesty, fraud, deceit or misrepresentation; (d) Reserved; (e) state or imply an ability to influence improperly a government agency or official; or (f) knowingly assist a judge or judicial officer in conduct that is a violation of applicable rules of judicial conduct or other law; or (g) fail to cooperate during the course of an ethics investigation or disciplinary proceeding.

4. Contempt of Court under HRS 710-1077:
 What It States: HRS 710-1077 addresses contempt of court, including willful disobedience of procedural rules and court orders.

HI Rev Stat  710-1077 (2023) 710-1077 Criminal contempt of court. (1) A person commits the offense of criminal contempt of court if:
(a) The person recklessly engages in disorderly or contemptuous behavior, committed during the sitting of a court in its immediate view and presence, and directly tending to interrupt its proceedings or impair the respect due to its authority;
(b) The person creates a breach of peace or a disturbance with intent to interrupt a court's proceedings; (c) As an attorney, clerk, or other officer of the court, the person knowingly fails to perform or violates a duty of the person's office, or knowingly disobeys a lawful directive or order of a court; (d) The person knowingly publishes a false report of a court's proceedings; (e) Knowing that the person is not authorized to practice law, the person represents the person's self to be an attorney and acts as such in a court proceeding;
(f) The person intentionally records or attempts to record the deliberation of a jury; (g) The person knowingly disobeys or resists the process, injunction, or other mandate of a court; (h) The person intentionally refuses to be qualified as a witness in any court or, after being qualified, to answer any proper interrogatory without a privilege to refuse to answer;
(i) Being a juror, the person intentionally, without permission of the court, fails to attend a trial or official proceeding to which the person has been summoned or at which the person has been chosen to serve; or (j) The person is in violation or disobedience of any injunction or order expressly provided for in part V of chapter 712.

(2) Except as provided in subsections (3) and (7), criminal contempt of court is a misdemeanor.

(3) The court may treat the commission of an offense under subsection (1) as a petty misdemeanor, in which case: (a) If the offense was committed in the immediate view and presence of the court, or under such circumstances that the court has knowledge of all of the facts constituting the offense, the court may order summary conviction and disposition;
 Violation: Opposing counsels deliberate delays and procedural misconduct amount to disobedience of the courts authority.

 Impact: Such behavior not only disrespects the judicial process but also undermines the court's ability to enforce its own rules.

IN THE FAMILY COURT OF THE FIRST CIRCUIT STATE OF HAWAII 5. Breach of Good Faith and Accuracy under Contract Law Principles (Restatement (Second) of Contracts
 202 and UCC  1-304):
 What It States: Legal documents must be prepared and executed in good faith, with accurate representations.

Restatement Second of Contracts  202
Rules in Aid of Interpretation
Words and other conduct are interpreted in the light of all the circumstances, and if the principal purpose of the parties is ascertainable it is given great weight.

A writing is interpreted as a whole, and all writings that are part of the same transaction are interpreted together.

Unless a different intention is manifested,
where language has a generally prevailing meaning, it is interpreted in accordance with that meaning; technical terms and words of art are given their technical meaning when used in a transaction within their technical field.

Where an agreement involves repeated occasions for performance by either party with knowledge of the nature of the performance and opportunity for objection to it by the other, any course of performance accepted or acquiesced in without objection is given great weight in the interpretation of the agreement.

Wherever reasonable, the manifestations of intention of the parties to a promise or agreement are interpreted as consistent with each other and with any relevant course of performance, course of dealing, or usage of trade.

Uniform Commercial Code Law Section 1-304
Obligation of Good Faith
Section 1--304. Obligation of Good Faith. Every contract or duty within this act imposes an obligation of good faith in its performance and enforcement.

Source: Section 1-304  Obligation of Good Faith, https://www.-nysenate.-gov/legislation/laws/UCC/1-304
(updated Dec. 26, 2014; accessed Dec. 21, 2024).

 Violation: The decree contained material errors, including misspelled names, incorrect dates, and grammatical mistakes, reflecting a lack of diligence and good faith. Furthermore, the integrity of the draft is entirely and totally fractured from start to finish.

Comes now the Movant, CASEY DEL CARPIO BARTON], pro se, submits this Motion to Quash the Rule 58 Submission filed by opposing counsel, find contempt of court for procedural violations, and request sanctions for egregious conduct. This motion is based on the following grounds: 1. Opposing counsel violated the 10-day submission requirement under HFCR Rule 58(b) by delaying submission for 37 days without justification or leave of court, an unprecedented delay that undermines procedural integrity.

2. Procedural fairness was further obstructed when the notice was served on Thanksgiving Day, a federal holiday, violating HFCR Rule 6(a), which defers deadlines to the next business day.

3. The submitted decree was rife with material errors, including egregious grammatical mistakes, misspelled names, and incorrect dates, demonstrating a lack of diligence and good faith.

4. Opposing counsels deliberate misrepresentation of submission dates and disregard for court orders constitutes ethical violations under HRPC Rules 3.4 and 8.4 and reflects vexatious litigation and coercive control.

5. Under principles of contract law, a decree riddled with such errors and omissions is nullified, as the foundational elements of accuracy and good faith were absent. See Restatement (Second) of Contracts 202 and UCC1-304 (obligation of good faith in performance).

6. The cumulative actions of opposing counsel amount to contempt of court under HRS 710-1077, warranting immediate judicial intervention.

IN THE FAMILY COURT OF THE FIRST CIRCUIT STATE OF HAWAII MEMORANDUM IN SUPPORT OF MOTION
I. INTRODUCTION
This motion arises from gross procedural and ethical violations committed by opposing counsel, Scot Brower, whose conduct undermines the dignity of this Court and causes substantial harm to the Movant and the minor child, Kekoa. The extraordinary delay in submission, combined with the decrees blatant errors and coercive tactics, constitutes contempt of court and warrants significant sanctions.

II. FACTUAL BACKGROUND
1. Unprecedented Delay: Opposing counsel submitted the decree 37 days post-hearing, THIRTY
SEVEN DAYS POST HEARING. Iin clear violation of HFCR Rule 58(b). This delay far exceeds any reasonable timeframe and exemplifies extreme bad faith.

2. Holiday Obstruction: The court filing of Rule 58 submission was submitted and served on me on Thanksgiving Day, a deliberate act to impose intimidation and curtail the Movants ability to respond, violating HFCR Rule 6(a).

3. Egregious Errors: The decree contained numerous errors, including:
 Misspelled names, including the judges name and the Movants name.

 Incorrect dates, falsely claiming submission on September 3, 2024, when in fact it was submitted on August 31, 2024. MANIPULATION OF TRIBUNAL
 Grammatical mistakes that undermine the credibility and enforceability of the document.

4. Coercive Conduct: Opposing counsel refused to substantively engage with the Movant, instructing them to sign and return without addressing the decrees numerous flaws. The latest in a long line of expression of disinterest and a refusal to progress.

5. Harm to the Minor Child: Procedural delays and ongoing misconduct exacerbate the emotional and physical harm to Kekoa, who continues to suffer under these protracted proceedings. I HAVE EXPRESSED
TO THE JUDGE MORE THAN FOUR TIMES OUR SON SUFFERED A BROKE ARM BUT IT IS FALLING ON
DEAF EARS AND TRAPPED IN FRIVOLOUS PREFERENCE OF FORM.

Hawaii Revised Statutes 710-1077  Criminal contempt of court
Current as of: 2024 | Check for updates | Other versions
(1) A person commits the offense of criminal contempt of court if: Attorney's Note
Under the Hawaii Revised Statutes, punishments for crimes depend on the classification. In the case of this section:
Class
Prison
Fine
misdemeanor
up to 1 year
$2,000
petty misdemeanor
up to 30 days
up to $1,000
For details, see Haw. Rev. Stat.  706-663

Terms Used In Hawaii Revised Statutes 710-1077
(a) The person recklessly engages in disorderly or contemptuous behavior, committed during the sitting of a court in its immediate view and presence, and directly tending to interrupt its proceedings or impair the respect due to its authority; (b) The person creates a breach of peace or a disturbance with intent to interrupt a courts proceedings;
(c) As an attorney, clerk, or other officer of the court, the person knowingly fails to perform or violates a duty of the persons office, or knowingly disobeys a lawful directive or order of a court; (d) The person knowingly publishes a false report of a courts proceedings; (e) Knowing that the person is not authorized to practice law, the person represents the persons self to be an attorney and acts as such in a court proceeding; (f) The person intentionally records or attempts to record the deliberation of a jury; (g) The person knowingly disobeys or resists the process, injunction, or other mandate of a court; (h) The person intentionally refuses to be qualified as a witness in any court or, after being qualified, to answer any proper interrogatory without a privilege to refuse to answer; (i) Being a juror, the person intentionally, without permission of the court, fails to attend a trial or official proceeding to which the person has been summoned or at which the person has been chosen to serve; or(j) The person is in violation or disobedience of any injunction or order expressly provided for in part V of chapter 712. (2) Except as provided in subsections (3) and (7), criminal contempt of court is a misdemeanor. (3) The court may treat the commission of an offense under subsection (1) as a petty misdemeanor, in which case:
(a) If the offense was committed in the immediate view and presence of the court, or under such circumstances that the court has knowledge of all of the facts constituting the offense, the court may order summary conviction and disposition; and(b) If the offense was not committed in the immediate view and presence of the court, nor under such circumstances that the court has knowledge of all of the facts constituting the offense, the court shall order the defendant to appear before it to answer a charge of criminal contempt of court; the trial, if any, upon the charge shall be by the court without a jury; and proof of guilt beyond a reasonable doubt shall be required for conviction.

(4) When the contempt under subsection (1) also constitutes another offense, the contemnor may be charged with and convicted of the other offense notwithstanding the fact that the contemnor has been charged with or convicted of the contempt. (5) Whenever any person is convicted of criminal contempt of court or sentenced therefor, the particular circumstances of the offense shall be fully set forth in the judgment and in the order or warrant of commitment. In any proceeding for review of the judgment, sentence, or commitment, no presumption of law shall be made in support of the jurisdiction to render the judgment, pronounce the sentence, or order the commitment. A judgment, sentence, or commitment under subsection (3)(a) shall not be subject to review by appeal, but shall be subject to review in an appropriate proceeding for an extraordinary writ or in a special proceeding for review.

All other judgments, sentences, or commitments for criminal contempt of court shall be subject to review by appeal, in a proceeding for an appropriate extraordinary writ, or in a special proceeding for review.

(6) Nothing in this section shall be construed to alter the courts power to punish civil contempt. When the contempt consists of the refusal to perform an act which the contemnor has the power to perform, the contemnor may be imprisoned until the contemnor has performed it. In such a case the act shall be specified in the warrant of commitment. In any proceeding for review of the judgment or commitment, no presumption of law shall be made in support of the jurisdiction to render the judgment or order the commitment. When a court of competent jurisdiction issues an order compelling a parent to furnish support, including child support, medical support, or other remedial care, for the parents child, it shall constitute prima facie evidence of a civil contempt of court upon proof that:
16


IN THE FAMILY COURT OF THE FIRST CIRCUIT STATE
OF HAWAII
(a) The order was made, filed, and served on the parent or proof that the parent was present in court at the time the order was pronounced; and(b) The parent did not comply with the order.

An order of civil contempt of court based on prima facie evidence under this subsection shall clearly state that the failure to comply with the order of civil contempt of court may subject the parent to a penalty that may include imprisonment or, if imprisonment is immediately ordered, the conditions that must be met for release from imprisonment. A party may also prove civil contempt of court by means other than prima facie evidence under this subsection.

(7) Any violation or disobedience of any injunction or order expressly provided for in part V of chapter 712 is punishable by:
(a) A fine of not less than $400 nor more than $5,000; (b) Imprisonment for not less than one nor more than six months; or(c) Both a fine and imprisonment pursuant to paragraphs (a) and (b).

Hawaii Revised Statutes (HRS)
HRS  710-1077 - Criminal Contempt of Court
 Text of the Law (Paraphrased): This statute penalizes individuals for willfully disobeying or resisting lawful court orders, thereby undermining the authority or proper functioning of the judiciary.

 Application:
o
The court can impose sanctions, including monetary penalties or other corrective actions, to deter and address misconduct.

o
Opposing counsels willful delay (37 days) and repeated procedural violations directly contravene this statute.


Hawaii Family Court Rules (HFCR)
HFCR Rule 58(b) - Timeliness of Draft Orders
 Text of the Rule: The prevailing party shall prepare a judgment, decree, or order in accordance with the courts decision within ten (10) days, unless otherwise directed by the court.
 Application:
o
Opposing counsels failure to adhere to the 10-day timeframe by submitting a draft decree 37 days after the hearing violates this rule.

o
The absence of a valid explanation further aggravates this procedural breach.

HFCR Rule 58(c) - Monetary Sanctions for Defective Submissions
 Text of the Rule (Paraphrased): A party who submits a defective or untimely judgment, decree, or order may be subject to monetary sanctions as deemed appropriate by the court.
 Application:
o
Opposing counsels submission of a flawed and untimely decree invites sanctions under this provision.

o
The defective decree contained errors in names, dates, and other critical details, and the holiday notice compounded the misconduct.

HFCR Rule 11(b) - Prohibition Against Bad Faith Filings


 Text of the Rule (Paraphrased): All filings must be made in good faith and not for improper purposes

such as to harass, cause unnecessary delay, or increase litigation costs.

 Application:

o
Opposing counsels dismissive communication (e.g., a five-word email, sign and return) without

substantive engagement demonstrates bad faith.


o
Serving notice on Thanksgiving Day reflects a lack of respect for procedural fairness and good

faith.



Hawaii Rules of Profe
ssional Conduct (HRPC)

HRPC Rule 3.4 - Fairn
ess to Opposing Party




Text of the Rule (Paraphrased): A lawyer shall not obstruct another partys access to evidence or knowingly disobey an obligation under tribunal rules, nor shall they act in a manner intended to delay proceedings or unfairly prejudice the opposing party.
 Application:
o
Opposing counsels disregard for timely and meaningful communication, combined with procedural delays, constitutes unfair treatment of a pro se litigant.

o
Failing to provide an opportunity for substantive review further contravenes this rule.

HRPC Rule 8.4 - Prohibition of Dishonesty, Fraud, and Misrepresentation
 Text of the Rule (Paraphrased): It is professional misconduct for a lawyer to engage in conduct involving dishonesty, fraud, deceit, or misrepresentation.
 Application:
o
The draft decree contained numerous errors and misrepresentations, including incorrect dates and names.

o
The biased nature of the draft decree demonstrates an intent to unfairly disadvantage the opposing party.

Case Law


In re Sanctions Against Earle A. Partington and Robert Patrick McPherson


 Key Holding: The Hawaii Supreme Court emphasized that procedural violations undermine judicial

integrity and justify sanctions.


 Application: Opposing counsels procedural breaches reflect a pattern of neglect that disrupts the orderly

administration of justice.


Stat

e v. Agdinaoay




Key Holding: Courts can hold individuals in contempt for failing to comply with procedural deadlines or lawful court orders.


 Application: Opposing counsels delay of 37 days, exceeding the 10-day rule, justifies a finding of contempt.



Sanctions and Contempt
 Judicial Authority: The court retains inherent authority to issue sanctions or hold individuals in contempt to preserve its integrity and deter future misconduct.

 Justifications for Sanctions Against Opposing Counsel:
o
Repeated procedural violations, including the 37-day delay.

o
Flawed submissions containing misrepresentations.

o
Failure to act professionally and fairly toward a pro se litigant.

SANCTIONS


COMES NOW, CASEY DEL CARPIO BARTON, pro se, and moves this Honorable Court to quash the Rule 58 submission iled by opposing counsel, Mr. Scot Brower, on 11/22/2024. This motion further seeks the imposition of sanctions against Mr. Brower for his blatant disregard for procedural integrity, repeated acts of misrepresentation, and persistent bad faith within family proceedings under the responsibility of childs best interest and toward a pro se litigant.


This Court must act to deter such egregious conduct, which undermines the administration of justice and public trust of Court.



**This motion arises from both the urgent need to protect the well-being of the minor child, KKDCB, and to address significant procedural misconduct by opposing counsel. KKDCB has recently endured severe physical injuries under circumstances suggesting neglect, including a fractured arm requiring surgery with titanium screws, he says many severe cuts resulting in substantial bleeding, and a second-degree burn sustained at his birthday party from an oven.



These incidents demonstrate a pattern of harm that necessitates immediate judicial intervention. The Childs Best Interest is the Foundation of What We Stand For.**

MEMORANDUM IN SUPPORT OF MOTION


I. INTRODUCTION


This motion arises from a pattern of deliberate misconduct and procedural violations by opposing counsel,


as evidenced by:


1. An unprecedented 37-day delay in submitting a Rule 58 draft decree, blatantly louting the court-ordered 10-day timeline mandated under Hawaii Family Court Rules (HFCR) Rule 58(b). Brower


submitted the Rule 58 Notice on the morning of the Sixth day; Thanksgiving. No observance of his own


massive personal failure. Furthermore, Undersigned Party submitted a motion in response to my


disagreement with procedural alignment and unreasonable substance within. No Money, No credibility,


and No Reason is not something that should ever be included in a decree  it is engineered for


humiliation and inluencing the next tribunals. These are very bad faith intentions on which you are


unable to decree upon anybody.



2. Gross inaccuracies in the draft, including misspelling the presiding judges name, the undersigneds


name totally wrong, and misstating the iling initiation date, all of which relect negligence and

contempt for accuracy. Brower conducted manipulation of the court by stating September 3, 2024 as


the date the motion was submitted,. August 31 is the real day of submission.



3. Serving the notice of the decree on Thanksgiving Day, a national holiday for Family, which was a

calculated attempt to demoralize and burden. Although there are no laws against it, the judicial notice


is that it is an extremely adversarial act.

4. Utterly dismissive communication, wherein Mr. Brower merely instructed me to sign and return, LJ

displaying contemptuous disregard for legal procedure and professional courtesy.

II. FACTUAL BACKGROUND


1.

This motion arises from a pattern of deliberate misconduct and procedural violations by opposing counsel, as evidenced within the docket itself. Expansion is easy.



2.

An unprecedented 37-day delay in submitting a Rule 58 draft decree, blatantly


louting the court-ordered 10-day timeline mandated under Hawaii Family Court Rules (HFCR) Rule 58(b).



3.

Gross inaccuracies in the draft, including misspelling the presiding judges name, the undersigneds name, and misstating the iling initiation date, all of which relect negligence and contempt for accuracy.



4.

Serving the notice of the decree on Thanksgiving Day, a national holiday, which was a calculated attempt to deny the undersigned a fair opportunity to respond.



5.

Utterly dismissive communication, wherein Mr. Brower merely instructed me to


sign and return, displaying contemptuous disregard for legal procedure and professional courtesy.
